        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248"><meta property="og:title" content="Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/acsomega.4c06248.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="The abundance of raw materials is a significant advantage that positions sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as a promising energy storage solution for the future. However, the low cycle efficiency and poor rate capacity of cathode materials have hindered the commercialization of SIBs, prompting extensive research efforts to address these challenges. Ion doping into the material structure is considered to be an effective, simple, and scalable approach to enhancing the electrical performance of cathode materials. In this work, B and F elemental ions were selectively doped into the structure of sodium-lithium-manganese-cobalt oxide material via the sol–gel method combined with calcination. The effects of B and F ion doping on the properties of the obtained materials exhibited distinct variations, particularly in the electrochemical performance. While the B-doped material (B-NLMC) exhibited a specific capacity of up to 166.5 mAh g–1 at a current density of 10 mA g–1 and maintained 72.1% capacity after 100 cycles, the material simultaneously doped with B and F ions (BF-NLMC) demonstrated lower specific capacity and cycling efficiency compared to B-NLMC. However, the BF-NLMC material exhibited significantly improved rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of up to approximately 80 mAh g–1 at a high current density of 200 mA g–1. Obviously, this research offers valuable insights into diversifying doping strategies to enhance the electrochemical performance of cathode materials, contributing to the advancement of SIB technology."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/acsomega.4c06248.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="9318a7bbcdb0222a-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="9318a7bbcdb0222a-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '6e4982ca-a7e2-4f47-991a-87907abcdb86'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/requestidlecallback-polyfill-f5170b9de43ccc25622c.js"></script><script charset="utf-8" async="" src="https://script.hotjar.com/modules.f98993dba31a932bc912.js"></script><script id="yui__dyn_0" type="text/javascript" src="https://www2.snapengage.com/chatjs/ServiceGetConfig?w=921a4ec7-cecf-43a6-afa5-6cd1346520b1"></script><script charset="utf-8" src="https://pubs.acs.org/products/achs/releasedAssets/js/lazy-imports-6922fe6a4ca6b2e0cd9a.js"></script><script type="text/javascript" src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

        });</script><style type="text/css">.MathJax_Hover_Frame {border-radius: .25em; -webkit-border-radius: .25em; -moz-border-radius: .25em; -khtml-border-radius: .25em; box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -webkit-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -moz-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; -khtml-box-shadow: 0px 0px 15px #83A; border: 1px solid #A6D ! important; display: inline-block; position: absolute}

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="9318a7bbcdb0222a-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'omega';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/omega/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/omega/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="9318a7bbcdb0222a-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "acsodf";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Development of Sodium-Lithium-Manganese-Cobalt Oxide with B Doping or B/F Dual Doping as Cathode Electrode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsomega.4c06248", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

These metrics are regularly updated to reflect usage leading up to the last few days.</p><p>Citations are the number of other articles citing this article, calculated by Crossref and updated daily.<a href="https://www.crossref.org/services/cited-by/"> Find more information about Crossref citation counts.</a></p><p>The Altmetric Attention Score is a quantitative measure of the attention that a research article has received online. Find more information on<a href="https://help.altmetric.com/support/solutions/articles/6000233311-how-is-the-altmetric-attention-score-calculated"> the Altmetric Attention Score and how the score is calculated.</a></p></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/medium/ao4c06248_0010.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/large/ao4c06248_0010.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsomega.4c06248&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">The abundance of raw materials is a significant advantage that positions sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as a promising energy storage solution for the future. However, the low cycle efficiency and poor rate capacity of cathode materials have hindered the commercialization of SIBs, prompting extensive research efforts to address these challenges. Ion doping into the material structure is considered to be an effective, simple, and scalable approach to enhancing the electrical performance of cathode materials. In this work, B and F elemental ions were selectively doped into the structure of sodium-lithium-manganese-cobalt oxide material via the sol–gel method combined with calcination. The effects of B and F ion doping on the properties of the obtained materials exhibited distinct variations, particularly in the electrochemical performance. While the B-doped material (B-NLMC) exhibited a specific capacity of up to 166.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a current density of 10 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and maintained 72.1% capacity after 100 cycles, the material simultaneously doped with B and F ions (BF-NLMC) demonstrated lower specific capacity and cycling efficiency compared to B-NLMC. However, the BF-NLMC material exhibited significantly improved rate capability, delivering a specific capacity of up to approximately 80 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 200 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Obviously, this research offers valuable insights into diversifying doping strategies to enhance the electrochemical performance of cathode materials, contributing to the advancement of SIB technology.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under</p><div class="article__cc-license__inter"><div class="article__cc-license--hoverable"><a href="https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-nd/4.0/" aria-describedby="tooltip-cc-text-abstract" class="link--bold" data-id="article_abstract_CC-License">CC-BY-NC-ND 4.0
                                    <span class="arrow"></span></a>
                                .

                                                </p></div></div></div></li><li class="article__cc-license__item"><a aria-describedby="tooltip-cc-1" class="article__cc-license__link" data-id="article_abstract_CC-License_IconBY"><span class="arrow"></span><img src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/images/cc-license/by.svg" alt="by licence" width="22" height="22" class="article__cc-license__icon"></a><div role="tooltip" id="tooltip-cc-1" class="article__hover" data-id="article_abstract_BY-IconTooltip"><div class="article__tooltip"><h3>License Summary*</h3><p>You are free to <span class="bold">share</span>(copy and redistribute)

Published by American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291484&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Diffraction"> Diffraction </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290714&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Doping"> Doping </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290667&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Ions"> Ions </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292506&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Materials"> Materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292316&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Transition metals"> Transition metals </a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">1.  Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The scarcity of raw materials and the constantly increasing cost of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have motivated humanity to strive to find new energy storage devices such as sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1" aria-label="reference 1">(1)</a> magnesium-ion batteries, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref2" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref2" aria-label="reference 2">(2)</a> fuel cells, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> zinc-air batteries, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref4" aria-label="reference 4">(4)</a> etc. In the groups, SIBs are considered to have a great commercial potential because of a high degree of similarity in structure, working mechanism, and research approach compared to LIBs. Therefore, the number of studies related to SIBs is constantly increasing and mainly focuses on cathode materials. The cathode materials for SIBs have several main groups such as layered structural oxide, pyrophosphate, and Prussian blue. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6 ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref6 ref7" aria-label="reference 5 to 7">(5−7)</a> Among them, the layered structural oxide materials are receiving special attention because of their high theoretical capacity, facile synthesis, and low cost; <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7" aria-label="reference 7">(7)</a> their general formula is Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MO<sub>2</sub>, where M is the symbol for transition metal ions such as Mn, Co, Ni, Fe, or their mixture.</div><div class="NLM_p">The layered structural oxide materials can be categorized into two primary groups: O3 type and P2 type. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref8" aria-label="reference 7 and 8">(7,8)</a> The phase change in the sodium-ion intercalation/deintercalation process is inevitable for both P2- and O3-type phases. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9" aria-label="reference 9">(9)</a> Meanwhile, the phase transformation of the O3-type structure is much more complex than that of the P2-type structure, leading to the P2-type structure material exhibiting better cycling performance. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref9 ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 9 and 10">(9,10)</a> However, the initial sodium content in the P2-type structure is lower than that in the O3-type structure, leading to their smaller specific capacities. Therefore, developing P2-type structure materials with high sodium content has received significant attention in efforts to bring SIBs into practical applications.</div><div class="NLM_p">The results revealed that the poor rate capacity and cycle performance have hindered the path to bringing SIBs into practical application. For example, material O3-NaMnO<sub>2</sub> delivers a specific capacity of 185 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C and retains of 71% of its initial capacity after 20 cycles, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11" aria-label="reference 11">(11)</a> O3-NaNiO<sub>2</sub> exhibits a specific capacity of 131 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C and approximately 15% initial capacity reduction after 5 cycles, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref12" aria-label="reference 12">(12)</a> P2-Na<sub>0.6</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> synthesized by the sol–gel method presents a specific capacity of 140 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C but only retains 53.6% after 9 cycles, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13" aria-label="reference 13">(13)</a> and P2-Na<sub>0.7</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> with a nanostructure demonstrates a specific capacity of up to 135 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 C and remains below 50% capacity after 100 cycles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref14" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref14" aria-label="reference 14">(14)</a> Overall, the limitations of material Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MO<sub>2</sub> stem from three main reasons: (i) the large size of sodium ions leading to limited kinetics of the sodium-ion intercalation/deintercalation process, (ii) irreversible phase change processes, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref15" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref7 ref15" aria-label="reference 7 and 15">(7,15)</a> and (iii) negative reactions between the active material and the electrolyte at high voltages. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16,17)</a> Based on that, numerous solutions have been implemented to address the above challenges such as protecting the material surface with a conductive coating or oxide to reduce unwanted reactions at high voltages, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 18 and 19">(18,19)</a> doping other ions such as Li<sup>+</sup>, Mg<sup>2+</sup>, Ti<sup>4+</sup>, Zn<sup>2+</sup>, etc., into the transition metal sites, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref20 ref21 ref22 ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 20 to 24">(20−24)</a> and diversifying various types of transition metal ion centers. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref25 ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 23, 25 and 26">(23,25,26)</a> While the solution of protecting the material surface requires more advanced techniques and many stages, the doping ion solution is simpler and easier to deploy on a large scale. Therefore, research into doping ions into the structure of materials to improve electrochemical performance is of more interest. For instance, Sehrawat and colleagues doped Li and Cu into the P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> material structure. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a> The expansion of the unit cell volume and the small volume change during the charging and discharging processes indicate why P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> materials with Li/Cu doping exhibit superior cycling performance compared to pristine P2-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. In another study, Xu and colleagues investigated the effect of Ti doping on the structural and electrochemical performance of O3-Na(Ni<sub>0.3</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>)<sub>1–<i>x</i></sub>Ti<sub><i>x</i></sub>O<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref21" aria-label="reference 21">(21)</a> Na(Ni<sub>0.3</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>)<sub>0.9</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exhibited excellent rate capacity with a specific capacity of 93 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 10 C and good cycling performance with 87.5% capacity retention after 300 cycles at a current density of 1C. The authors point out two reasons for the improved electrochemical performance of the Ti-doped materials: (i) the Ti doping widened the gap between MO<sub>2</sub> layers (M = transition metals), which allowed the sodium-ion intercalation/deintercalation process to be more favorable; (ii) the Ti doping elements also effectively prevented the P3–O3 phase transition. Besides doping with cations, anion doping such as F<sup>–</sup> has also been considered to enhance the electrochemical performance of cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 28 to 31">(28−31)</a> As reports have shown, a suitable amount of F<sup>–</sup> anion replacing the position of O<sup>2–</sup> anion allows widening the distance between transition metal layers and reducing the activation energy of the Na<sup>+</sup> ion migration process, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30 ref31" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30 ref31" aria-label="reference 30 and 31">(30,31)</a> which make the process of interleaving/deinterlacing Na<sup>+</sup> ions easier, and therefore, the electrochemical performance of the resulting material is enhanced, especially the rate capacity. Recently, simultaneous doping of both cations and anions into layered structural oxide materials has also been carried out such as Ti/F-codoped P2-Na<sub>0.7</sub>MnO<sub>2.05</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> Al/F-dual-doped P2-type sodium manganese oxide, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> and Mo–F-dual-doped O3-NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> Despite the promising approach, the number of studies following this research direction is relatively sparse, necessitating further efforts to comprehensively evaluate the efficacy of this solution and elucidate the underlying mechanisms driving the enhanced electrochemical performance.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this study, sodium-lithium-manganese-cobalt oxide materials with a P2-type layered structure doped with either boron (B-NLMC) or a combination of boron and fluorine (BF-NLMC) have been successfully synthesized. The comprehensive evaluation of the electrochemical performance of these materials revealed the profound impact of dopant elements on their energy storage capabilities. The incorporation of boron into the B-NLMC lattice resulted in an exceptional energy storage capacity of up to 166.5 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, which was maintained at 72.1% after 100 charge–discharge cycles at a current density of 10 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. While the BF-NLMC sample exhibited a slightly lower energy storage capacity and cycling performance compared to B-NLMC, it demonstrated a significant improvement in rate capability. At a high current density of 200 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, the BF-NLMC sample delivered a specific capacity of up to approximately 80 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>, which is approximately 260% higher than that of the B-NLMC sample. This study provides compelling evidence that B and F are promising dopants for improving the electrochemical performance of cathode materials. By optimizing the B/F ratio, it is believed that even better performing materials can be developed, paving the way for the advancement of high-energy and high-power energy storage systems.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">2.  Experimental Details</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.1.  Chemicals</h3><div class="NLM_p last">All chemicals used for this work include sodium carbonate (Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>), lithium fluoride (LiF), lithium carbonate (Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>), boric acid (H<sub>3</sub>BO<sub>3</sub>), manganese acetate tetrahydrate (Mn(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>·4H<sub>2</sub>O), cobalt acetate tetrahydrate (Co(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>·4H<sub>2</sub>O), citric acid monohydrate (C<sub>6</sub>H<sub>8</sub>O<sub>7</sub>), sodium metal (Na), sodium perchlorate (NaClO<sub>4</sub>), carbon black (Super P), polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF), <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidone (NMP), ethylene carbonate (EC), and diethyl carbonate (DC).</div></div><div id="sec2_2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.2.  Material Preparation</h3><div class="NLM_p last">In the present investigation, a detail-oriented synthesis approach utilizing the sol–gel method was employed to fabricate the materials of interest. The synthesis process involved a series of precisely controlled steps to ensure the formation of high-quality materials with tailored properties. Initially, a mixture comprising 16.8 mmol of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, 4.0 mmol of LiF, 32.0 mmol of Mn(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>·4H<sub>2</sub>O, 2.0 mmol of Co(CH<sub>3</sub>COO)<sub>2</sub>·4H2O, and 2 mmol of H<sub>3</sub>BO<sub>3</sub> was dissolved in a 150 mL solution containing 45 mmol of citric acid monohydrate. This solution underwent magnetic stirring at 500 rpm for 60 min to achieve homogeneity. Subsequently, the solution was subjected to continued magnetic stirring and heating at 100 °C until a gel phase was formed. The gel was then further treated by heating at 150 °C for 2 h to produce an aerogel, followed by a thermal treatment at 400 °C for 3 h to eliminate any residual carbon content. The resulting solid mixture underwent manual grinding in a zirconia mortar for 30 min before being subjected to a final heat treatment at 850 °C for 20 h to yield the desired material, designated as “BF-NLMC”, which exhibited simultaneous doping with B and F. Furthermore, the synthesis of sodium-lithium-manganese-cobalt oxide doped with B, denoted as “B-NLMC”, followed a similar procedure to that of BF-NLMC synthesis. However, in this case, the precursor LiF was substituted with 2 mmol of Li<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> to achieve the desired doping configuration.</div></div><div id="sec2_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.3.  Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p">Characteristic properties of materials are elucidated through a variety of sophisticated analytical techniques, including X-ray diffraction (XRD), scanning electron microscopy (SEM), scanning electron microscopy equipped with an energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy probe (SEM-EDX), transmission electron microscopy (TEM), high-resolution TEM (HR-TEM), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS), and inductively coupled plasma mass spectrometry (ICP-MS). These cutting-edge methods allow for a comprehensive understanding of the structural, microstructural, and chemical compositions of materials.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Valuable insights into the energy storage capabilities and stability of the synthesized materials, which are crucial for the development of high-performance energy storage devices, were carefully conducted using a CR2032-type sodium-ion battery (half-cell) using advanced techniques such as cyclic voltammetry (CV), galvanostatic charge–discharge (GCD), galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT), and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). The CR2032-type sodium-ion battery comprises a working electrode constructed from an active material serving as the cathode, a sodium foil functioning as the anode, a PP film as the separator, and a 1 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> solution as the electrolyte. The preparation of the working electrode follows the methodology outlined in ref  <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18" aria-label="reference 18">(18)</a>, where the mass ratio of active material, binder (PVDF), and conductive agent (Super P) is maintained at 80:10:10. Each electrode contains approximately 6–8 mg of active material. This comprehensive approach ensures the reproducibility and reliability of the experimental results, paving the way for further advancements in materials science and energy storage technology.</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">3.  Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec3_1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i8" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i8">3.1.  Characteristic Properties</h3><div class="NLM_p">The crystal structure of the materials was determined using X-ray diffraction (XRD) characterizations on a Bruker D8 machine with Cu–K<sub>α1</sub> radiation (∼0.15418 nm) at a rotation speed of 30 rpm, in a θ–2θ configuration, with a scanning step of approximately 0.03°, and in a characterization range spanning from 10 to 70°. The diffraction patterns of the synthesized B-NLMC and BF-NLMC materials revealed the presence of a P2 structure (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>a), agreeing well with the hexagonal crystal system and space group <i>P</i>63/<i>mmc</i> (Na<sub>0.7</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>-type, JCPDS #27-0571), at which the alkali metal exhibited trigonal prismatic coordination. The diffraction patterns exhibited minimal differences in peak number and position between the two materials, with peaks corresponding to oriented diffraction planes (002), (004), (100), (101), (102), (103), (104), (106), (110), (112), and (008) of a single hexagonal P2-type phase observed around 15.78, 31.90, 36.10, 37.04, 39.63, 43.70, 48.94, 62.11, 64.94, 66.75, and 67.31°, respectively.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/medium/ao4c06248_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/large/ao4c06248_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. XRD analysis results of synthesized materials: (a) XRD pattern, (b) Williamson–Hall plot, and (c, d) Rietveld refinement results.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsomega.4c06248/asset/images/large/ao4c06248_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsomega.4c06248&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To assess the impact of both B and F doping on the crystal structure of the sodium-lithium-manganese-cobalt oxide base material, Rietveld refinement was employed. The experimental and calculated XRD patterns for both materials agree well with this crystal system (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>b,d). Rietveld refinement utilized the Voigt pseudofunction to describe experimental diffraction data. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> The parameters <i>R</i><sub>wp</sub> (weighted profile factor) and χ<sup>2</sup> (goodness of fit) served as criteria to evaluate the refinement quality between the experimental and calculated data. The <i>R</i><sub>wp</sub>, χ<sup>2</sup> values for B-NLMC and BF-NLMC materials were (3.28%, 1.27) and (4.19%, 2.44), respectively, indicating high-quality refinement results. The diffraction spectrum displayed distinct sharp peaks, indicating that the synthesized materials are of high quality.</div><div class="NLM_p">Rietveld refinements were employed to identify the unit cell parameters of both P2 phases for both developed materials, i.e., (<i>a</i> = <i>b</i> ∼ 2.8681 Å, <i>c</i> ∼ 11.1995 Å, and <i>V</i> ∼ 79.78 Å<sup>3</sup>) and (<i>a</i> = <i>b</i> ∼ 2.8682 Å, <i>c</i> ∼ 11.1928 Å, and <i>V</i> ∼ 79.74 Å<sup>3</sup>) for B-NLMC and BF-NLMC materials, respectively. It implies that a small amount of F addition slightly changes the lattice parameters due to the difference in radii between F with 42 pm and B with 87 pm. The average crystallite size (<i>L</i>) and microstrain (ε) of the two material systems were evaluated using the Williamson–Hall method, which correlates these values with the full-width at half-maximum (β) of the X-ray diffraction (XRD) peaks. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> The β value is influenced by peak broadening of the measured sample, which is directly related to the nanocrystalline effect. However, XRD measurements can be affected by peak broadening from various sources, including the sample itself (such as crystal size, microstress, and homogeneity) and instrumental broadening (β<sub>i</sub>). To accurately evaluate the β value caused by the sample, β<sub>i</sub> must be eliminated using a standard powder sample, such as Al<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (SRM 676). The normalization process is detailed in the literature. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref37" aria-label="reference 37">(37)</a> The β value of the measured sample is primarily influenced by two main sources: the broadening due to crystallite size (β<sub>L</sub>) and the broadening due to microstrain (β<sub>s</sub>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref36" aria-label="reference 36">(36)</a> These values vary according to the Bragg diffraction angle (θ) as follows: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="ueq1"><div class="equation"><span class="MathJax_Preview" style="color: inherit;"><span class="MJXp-math MJXp-display" id="MJXp-Span-1"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-2"><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-3"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-4"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-5"><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-6"><span class="MJXp-mtable" id="MJXp-Span-7"><span><span class="MJXp-mtr" id="MJXp-Span-8" style="vertical-align: baseline;"><span class="MJXp-mtd" id="MJXp-Span-9" style="text-align: center;"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-10"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-11" style="margin-right: 0.05em;">β</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-12" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;">L</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-13"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-14" style="margin-left: 0.333em; height: 0em;"></span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-32">θ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="MJXp-mtr" id="MJXp-Span-33" style="vertical-align: baseline;"><span class="MJXp-mtd" id="MJXp-Span-34" style="padding-top: 0.861em; text-align: center;"><span class="MJXp-msub" id="MJXp-Span-35"><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-36" style="margin-right: 0.05em;">β</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-script" id="MJXp-Span-37" style="vertical-align: -0.4em;">s</span></span><span class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-38"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-39" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-40"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-41">4</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-42">ε</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-43">tan</span><span class="MJXp-mspace" id="MJXp-Span-44" style="width: 0.25em; height: 0em;"></span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-45">θ</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-1"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mstyle lineleading=".25ex" rowspacing="2ex"><mstyle indentshiftfirst="0em" indentshift="1em" indentshiftlast="1em"><mtable displaystyle="true"><mtr><mtd><msub><mi>β</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">L</mi></msub><mrow><mo>=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><mn>0.9</mn><msub><mi>λ</mi><mrow><mi>Cu</mi><mo>−</mo><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><msub><mi>α</mi><mn>1</mn></msub></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><mi>L</mi><mi>cos</mi><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><mi>θ</mi></mrow></mfrac></mstyle></mrow></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><msub><mi>β</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></msub><mrow><mo>=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mn>4</mn><mi>ε</mi><mi>tan</mi><mspace width="0.25em"></mspace><mi>θ</mi></mstyle></mrow></mtd></mtr></mtable></mstyle></mstyle></mstyle></mrow></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"></div></div>where 0.9 is the Scherrer constant. By understanding the contributions of these factors to peak broadening, a more accurate analysis of the material properties can be achieved. The dependence of β on β<sub>L</sub> and β<sub>s</sub> can be rewritten as follows: <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref38 ref39" class="MJXp-mrow" id="MJXp-Span-98"><span class="MJXp-mo" id="MJXp-Span-99" style="margin-left: 0.333em; margin-right: 0.333em;">=</span><span class="MJXp-mstyle" id="MJXp-Span-100"><span class="MJXp-mn" id="MJXp-Span-101">4</span><span class="MJXp-mi MJXp-italic" id="MJXp-Span-102">ε</span><span class="MJXp-mi" id="MJXp-Span-103">sin</span><span class="MJXp-mspace" id="MJXp-Span-104"
