                        cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon coated NaLi0.2Mn0.8O2 as a superb cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Quyen, Ngo Quy; Van Nguyen, To; Thang, Hoang Huu; Thao, Pham Manh; Van Nghia, Nguyen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2 structure materials have been known as a promising cathode material for sodium ion battery.  However, their substandard rate capability is a major obstacle for the application of sodium ion batteries to overcome.  Herein, we improved the rate capacity of the P2-type sodium-lithium-manganese oxide material by a carbon additive on the material surface.  The structure and morphol. of pristine sodium-lithium-manganese oxide (NLM) and carbon-coated sodium-lithium-manganese oxide (NLM@C) were confirmed by X-ray diffraction (XRD), Raman spectra, thermal gravimetric anal. (TGA), SEM and energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (SEM-EDS), and transmission electron microscopy (TEM).  The electrochem. results revealed that the carbon coating improves rate capability of NLM@C material and increases its specific capacity.  Specifically, the NLM@C material delivered a specific capacity of 160 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C, ca. 33% higher than that of pristine NLM material; the NLM@C material retained a capacity of 115 mAh g-1 at a high charged/discharged rate of 1 C.  The result suggests that NLM@C material is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b02555"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, D.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polypyrrole-Coated Sodium Manganate Hollow Microspheres as a Superior Cathode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Advanced electrode materials play a very important role in the development of large-scale prodn. of sodium-ion batteries.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Ti doping on the structural and electrochemical performance of O3-type Na(Ni0.3Fe0.2Mn0.5)1-xTixO2 cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Shuangwu; Chen, Hongxia; Li, Cheng; Nie, Rihuang; Yang, Yutian; Zhou, Mengcheng; Zhang, Xinyu; Zhou, Hongming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">962</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have shown great potential as energy storage devices due to their low price and abundant sodium content.  In terms of current research, cathode materials remain the bottleneck for improving the performance of SIBs.  Ti-doped O3-type Na(Ni0.3Fe0.2Mn0.5)1-xTixO2 (x = 0, 0.05, 0.1, 0.15) are investigated as the cathode material for sodium-ion batteries, and the results show that Ti doping can widen the layer spacing and suppress the ordering of Na+/vacancy and O3-P3 phase transition.  The structurally stable Na(Ni0.3Fe0.2Mn0.5)0.9Ti0.1O2 cathode material, in particular, demonstrates enhanced rate capacity (93 mAh g-1, 2.0-4.0 V vs Na+/Na, 10 C, and 115 mAh g-1, 2.0-4.2 V vs Na+/Na, 10 C) and excellent cycling stability (87.5% capacity retention, 2.0-4.0 V vs Na+/Na, after 300 cycles, 1 C, and 82.1% capacity retention, 2.0-4.2 V vs Na+/Na, after 100 cycles, 1 C).  In addn., Ti doping can effectively suppress the O3-P3 phase transition of the cathode materials and reduce the formation of the P3 phase at high voltage, which effectively suppresses the capacity decay during the charge/discharge process and reduces the irreversible capacity.  As a result, the Ti doping strategy provides a simple and effective method for designing and developing high-performance layered oxide cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01750A"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Clément, R.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structurally stable Mg-doped P2-Na2/3Mn1-yMgyO2 sodium-ion battery cathodes with high rate performance: insights from electrochemical, NMR and diffraction studies</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Clement, Raphaele J.; Billaud, Juliette; Robert Armstrong, A.; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo; Bruce, Peter G.; Grey, Clare P.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3240-3251</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a more sustainable alternative to the existing lithium-ion technol. and could alleviate some of the stress on the global lithium market as a result of the growing elec. car and portable electronics industries.  Fundamental research focused on understanding the structural and electronic processes occurring on electrochem. cycling is key to devising rechargeable batteries with improved performance.  We present an in-depth investigation of the effect of Mg doping on the electrochem. performance and structural stability of Na2/3MnO2 with a P2 layer stacking by comparing three compns.: Na2/3Mn1-yMgyO2 (y = 0.0, 0.05, 0.1).  We show that Mg substitution leads to smoother electrochem., with fewer distinct electrochem. processes, improved rate performance and better capacity retention.  These observations are attributed to the more gradual structural changes upon charge and discharge, as obsd. with synchrotron, powder X-ray, and neutron diffraction.  Mg doping reduces the no. of Mn3+ Jahn-Teller centers and delays the high voltage phase transition occurring in P2-Na2/3MnO2.  The local structure is investigated using 23Na solid-state NMR (ssNMR) spectroscopy.  The ssNMR data provide direct evidence for fewer oxygen layer shearing events, leading to a stabilized P2 phase, and an enhanced Na-ion mobility up to 3.8 V vs.  Na+/Na upon Mg doping.  The 5% Mg-doped phase exhibits one of the best rate performances reported to date for sodium-ion cathodes with a P2 structure, with a reversible capacity of 106 mA h g-1 at the very high discharge rate of 5000 mA g-1.  In addn., its structure is highly reversible and stable cycling is obtained between 1.5 and 4.0 V vs.  Na+/Na, with a capacity of approx. 140 mA h g-1 retained after 50 cycles at a rate of 1000 mA g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref23" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1007/s10008-023-05706-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Zinc doped P2-type layered cathode for high-voltage and long-life sodium ion batteries: impacts of calcination temperature and cooling methods</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting the reactivity of Ni2+/Ni3+ redox couple via fluorine doping of high performance Na0.6Mn0.95Ni0.05O2-xFx cathode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Hui; Wu, Zhenguo; Zhong, Yanjun; Chen, Tingru; Liu, Xiaohong; Qu, Jie; Xiang, Wei; Li, Juntao; Chen, Xianchun; Guo, Xiaodong; Zhong, Benhe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">308</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">64-73</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Though P2-type Na-Mn-Ni-O cathodes with low cost and environmental benign were extensively studied, it is still challenging to fulfill practical application with limited cycle stability and low operating potential.  However, the research of the reactive Ni2+/Ni3+ redox pair that enable both high working potential and high reversible capacity was almost ignored.  And traditional cationic doping mainly focuses on crystal modulation and structure stabilization.  An anion doping strategy (F-doping) was carried out to further boost the activity of Ni2+.  The multi-function including structural parameter modulation and robust Ni-F bond significantly promote the activation of Ni2+/Ni3+ and advance the resp. working potential.  Related reaction kinetics and structural evolution were also studied to elucidate the F-doping mechanism.  The Na0.6Mn0.95Ni0.05O1.95F0.05 with appropriate F content could deliver a high capacity of 80.76 mA h g-1 at 2C with 75.0% retained after 960 cycles.  The excellent rate capability and full cell performance also demonstrate the high potential.  This study may provide a new sight for the development of P2-type layered Na-Mn-Ni-O cathode, which could be extended to other oxides cathode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref31" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jssc.2021.122440"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">First-principles investigation on the crystal, electronic structures and diffusion barriers of F-doped NaMO2 (M = V, Cr, Co and Ni) for rechargeable Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">First-principles investigation on the crystal, electronic structures and diffusion barriers of F-doped NaMO2 (M=V, Cr, Co and Ni) for rechargeable Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Guobao; Zhu, Wuming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Solid State Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">302</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">First-principles calcns. based on d. functional theory (DFT) has been carried out to predict the structural stability, electronic structures and diffusion barrier of F-doped NaMO2 with stoichiometry of NaMO1.92F0.08 (M = V, Cr, Co and Ni).  Under this doping concn., it is found that F doping increases the structural stability of NaVO2, NaCrO2 and NaCoO2 for desodiation.  Also, F doping may significantly enhance electron cond. of NaMO2 (M = V, Cr, Co and Ni).  The nudged elastic band calcn. results indicate that F-doping lowers the diffusion barriers of NaVO2 and NaNiO2, which is beneficial to Na diffusion.  The results acquired are of benefit to promote the development of low-cost cathode materials with high performance for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref32" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.31635/renewables.022.202200012"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, P.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ti, F Codoped Sodium Manganate of Layered P2-Na0.7MnO2.05 Cathode for High Capacity and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Renewables</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">81</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">89</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anomalous Sodium Storage Behavior in Al/F Dual-Doped P2-Type Sodium Manganese Oxide Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chae, Munseok S.; Kim, Hyojeong J.; Lyoo, Jeyne; Attias, Ran; Gofer, Yosef; Hong, Seung-Tae; Aurbach, Doron</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Various types of sodium manganese oxides are promising cathode materials for sodium storage systems.  One of the most considerable advantages of this family of materials is their widespread natural abundance.  So far, only a few host candidates have been reported and there is a need to develop new materials with improved practical electrochem. performance.  Here, P2-type Al/F-doped sodium manganese oxide as well as its unique sodium storage mechanism is demonstrated by a combination of electrochem. characterization, structural analyses from powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) data, and 3D bond valence energy level calcns. for the sodium diffusion pathways.  The material exhibits a high reversible capacity of 164.3 mAh g-1 (0.3C rate) and capacity retention of 89.1% after 500 cycles (5C rate).  The study clearly unravels the beneficial effect of the doping and the unique sodium intercalation mechanism devoid of the low diffusion O3 transformation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1016/j.mtcomm.2022.103839"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High stability of Mo-F dual-doped O3-type NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode material for sodium-ion battery</span>. <i>Materials Today Communications</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>32</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">103839</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1107/S0021889869006558"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rietveld, H.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Profile refinement method for nuclear and magnetic structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rietveld, H. M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Applied Crystallography</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1969</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Pt. 2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">65-71</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACGAR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-8898</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">A structural refinement method for neutron diffraction is presented which makes direct use of the profile intensities obtained from the powder diagram.  It is applicable to nuclear structures and to magnetic structures which can be described on the nuclear unit cell or a multiple thereof.  Equations for the measured profiles to be used in the least sqs. treatment are cor. for asymmetry and preferred orientation; the angular dependence of the half widths of the peaks is given by the formula of Caglioti, et al. (1958).  The magnetic contribution to the profile equation is expressed by calcg. only one av. cross section for each set of equiv. reflections.  It is possible to introduce constraint functions, linear or quadratic, between parameters used in the least sqs. treatment.  Results of the use of this method are given for a series of compds.  In all instances it has proved superior to any other method involving integrated neutron powder intensities, single or overlapping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/0001-6160(53)90006-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Williamson, G. H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">X-ray line broadening from filed aluminium and wolfram</span>. <i>Acta Metall.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1953</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">1</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">22</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">31</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">X-ray line broadening from filed aluminum and tungsten</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Williamson, G. K.; Hall, W. H.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Acta Metallurgica</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1953</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">No. 1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">22-31</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AMETAR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-6160</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Methods of analysis previously used in the interpretation of line broadening are discussed and are shown to be inadequate; more reliable methods being outlined.  An analysis of published results by one of these methods suggests that the observed effects can be attributed to simultaneous small particle size and strain broadening.  Measurements of the changes in intensity distribution have been made, with a Geiger counter spectrometer, in the spectra of cold-worked Al and W.  The line breadths may be attributed to simultaneous small particle size and strain broadening, the latter predominating, particularly at the higher Bragg angles, and it is shown that the observed effects are produced by dislocations or some similar structural fault.  The observed rise in the breadths of the high angle lines from annealed materials suggests that some dislocations remain after annealing.  Fourier analysis of the line shapes in general merely confirm the results of the analysis of the line breadths, but in the case of the recovered specimens it suggests that the dislocations form into walls ("polygonization").</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2023.156756"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nguyen

                10.1021/acs.inorgchem.8b00284</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D57%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D5249-5257%26journal%3DInorg.%2BChem.%26issue%3D9%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26title%3DDifferent%2BEffects%2Bof%2BAl%2BSubstitution%2Bfor%2BMn%2Bor%2BFe%2Bon%2Bthe%2BStructure%2Band%2BElectrochemical%2BProperties%2Bof%2BNa0.67Mn0.5Fe0.5O2%2Bas%2Ba%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBattery%2BCathode%2BMaterial%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.inorgchem.8b00284&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.4c06248&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.inorgchem.8b00284&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Different Effects of Al Substitution for Mn or Fe on the Structure and Electrochemical Properties of Na0.67Mn0.5Fe0.5O2 as a Sodium Ion Battery Cathode Material</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Huibo; Gao, Rui; Li, Zhengyao; Sun, Limei; Hu, Zhongbo; Liu, Xiangfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Inorganic Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5249-5257</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">INOCAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0020-1669</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type layered oxides based on the elements Fe and Mn have attracted great interest as sodium ion battery (SIB) cathode materials owing to their inexpensive metal constituents and high specific capacity.  However, they suffer from rapid capacity fading and complicated phase transformations.  Here, we modulate the crystal structure and optimize the electrochem. performances of Na0.67Mn0.5Fe0.5O2 by Al doping for Mn or Fe, resp., and the roles of Al in the enhancement of the rate capability and cycling performance are unraveled.  The substitution of Al for Mn or Fe decreases the lattice parameters a and c but enlarges d spacing and lengthens Na-O bonds, which enhances Na+ diffusion and rate capability esp. for Na0.67Mn0.5Fe0.47Al0.03O2.  Al doping reduces the thickness of TMO2 and strengthens TM-O/O-O bonding.  This enhances the layered structure stability and the capacity retention.  Al doping mitigates Mn3+ and Jahn-Teller distortion, mitigating the irreversible phase transition.  Al doping also alleviates the lattice vol. variation and the structure strain.  This further improves the stability of the layered structure and the cycling performances particularly in the case of Al doping for Fe.  The in-depth insights into the roles of Al substitution might be also useful for designing high-performance cathode materials for SIBs through appropriate lattice doping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref45" class="refNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit45" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA05137G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soares, C.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na2.4Al0.4Mn2.6O7 anionic redox cathode material for sodium-ion batteries – a combined experimental and theoretical approach to elucidate its charge storage mechanism</span>. <i>Journal of Materials Chemistry A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">7341</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7356</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/D1TA05137G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D7341-7356%26journal%3DJournal%2Bof%2BMaterials%2BChemistry%2BA%26issue%3D13%26author%3DC.%2BSoares%26title%3DNa2.4Al0.4Mn2.6O7%2Banionic%2Bredox%2Bcathode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%2B%25E2%2580%2593%2Ba%2Bcombined%2Bexperimental%2Band%2Btheoretical%2Bapproach%2Bto%2Belucidate%2Bits%2Bcharge%2Bstorage%2Bmechanism%26doi%3D10.1039%252FD1TA05137G&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.4c06248&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FD1TA05137G&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na2.4Al0.4Mn2.6O7 anionic redox cathode material for sodium-ion batteries - a combined experimental and theoretical approach to elucidate its charge storage mechanism</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Soares, Cindy; Silvan, Begona; Choi, Yong-Seok; Celorrio, Veronica; Seymour, Valerie R.; Cibin, Giannantonio; Griffin, John M.; Scanlon, David O.; Tapia-Ruiz, Nuria</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">13</span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Here we report the synthesis via ceramic methods of the high-performance Mn-rich Na2.4Al0.4Mn2.6O7 oxygen-redox cathode material for Na-ion batteries, which we use as a testbed material to study the effects of Al substitution and subsequent Na excess in the high-capacity, anionic redox-based cathode material, Na2Mn3O7.  The material shows a stable electrochem. performance, with a specific capacity of 215 mA h g-1 in the 1.5-4.7 V voltage range at C/20 and a capacity retention of 90% after 40 cycles.  Using a combination of electrochem. and structural anal. together with hybrid d. functional theory calcns. we explain the behavior of this material with changes in Mn/anionic redox reactions and assocd. O2 release reactions occurring during electrochem. cycling (Na+ ion insertion/extn.), and compare these findings to Na2Mn3O7.  We expect that these results will advance understanding of the effect of dopants in Mn-rich cathode materials with oxygen redox activity to pave their way towards high-performance sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2018.06.050"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, S.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Novel P2-type concentration-gradient Na0.67Ni0.167Co0.167Mn0.67O2 modified by Mn-rich surface as cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Novel P2-type concentration-gradient Na0.67Ni0.167Co0.167Mn0.67O2 modified by Mn-rich surface as cathode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bao, Shuo; Luo, Shao-hua; Wang, Zhi-yuan; Yan, Sheng-xue; Wang, Qing; Li, Jia-yu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing rechargeable sodium ion batteries with high capacity and long cycle life is still a big challenge.  Herein, we present P2-type concn.-gradient material with av. compn. of Na0.67Ni0.167Co0.167Mn0.67O2, which exhibits relatively high discharge capacity and excellent stability.  The material delivers higher discharge capacity and better rate performance than that of the concn.-const. Na0.67Ni0.167Co0.167Mn0.67O2 during cycling.  Also, the material exhibits excellent capacity retention of ∼87% after 100 cycles.  The high discharge capacity is attributed to the Ni-rich core and the improvement in cycling stability is due to a gradual and continuous increase of Mn4+ in the concn.-gradient spherical particles.  The primary particles on the Mn-rich surface have smaller size than that of the const.-concn. samples, leading to a preferential cryst. state, therefore they can facilitate excellent transport properties for Na ions insertion/extn. process.  The P2-type concn.-gradient material provides a new way for the development of advanced sodium ion batteries with high capacity and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta01430d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, D.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synthesis and electrochemical behaviors of layered Na0.67[Mn0.65Co0.2Ni0.15]O2 microflakes as a stable cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Journal of Materials Chemistry A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3895</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3899</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis and electrochemical behavior of layered Na0.67[Mn0.65Co0.2Ni0.15]O2 microflakes as a stable cathode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Dingding; He, Wei; Pei, Feng; Wu, Fayuan; Wu, Yue; Qian, Jiangfeng; Cao, Yuliang; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stable Na+ storage cathodes with adequate reversible capacity are needed for enabling Na-ion battery technol. for large scale and low cost elec. storage.  In light of the superior Li+ storage performance of layered oxides, pure P2-phase Na0.67[Mn0.65Ni0.15Co0.2]O2 microflakes are synthesized by a simple sol-gel method and tested as a Na+ storage cathode.  These layered microflakes exhibit a considerably high reversible capacity of 141 mA h g-1 and a slow capacity decay to 125 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles, showing better cyclability than previous NaMnO2 compds.  To further enhance the structural and cycling stability, the authors partially substituted Co3+ by Al3+ in the transition-metal layer to synthesize Na0.67[Mn0.65Ni0.15Co0.15Al0.05]O2.  As expected, the Al-substituted material demonstrates a greatly improved cycling stability with a 95.4% capacity retention over 50 cycles, possibly serving as a high capacity and stable cathode for Na-ion battery applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1007/s11581-019-03035-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, L.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nb5+-doped P2-type Mn-based layered oxide cathode with an excellent high-rate cycling stability for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Ionics</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">10</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">4775</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4786</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nb5+-doped P2-type Mn-based layered oxide cathode with an excellent high-rate cycling stability for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Lijun; Wang, Yanzhi; Zhao, Jiabin; Li, Yanhong; Wang, Jinlong; Yang, Xiaheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Ionics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-Na0.67Co0.25Mn0.75-xNbxO2 (x = 0, 0.015, 0.030, 0.045) cathode materials were obtained by a simple solid-state method.  The Nb5+-doped effects on ameliorating the structural and electrochem. properties of the Na0.67Co0.25Mn0.75O2 parent material for sodium-ion batteries have been investigated.  XRD measurements confirm a hexagonal main phase (P63/mmc) and some trace of orthorhombic NaNbO3 (P21ma).  Rietveld refinements exhibit the higher lattice parameters and the bigger c/a values due to Nb5+ doping into the parent Na0.67Co0.25Mn0.75O2.  The optimized 3.0 at.% Nb5+-doped P2-Na0.67Co0.25Mn0.75O2 sample delivers the initial discharge capacity of 126.7 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C in the voltage range of 1.8-4.0 V, and its capacity retention is 75.3% after 100 cycles, which is 63.7% higher than that of the pristine.  Whereas at 10 C rate, the optimized sample presents the maximal discharge capacity of 72.8 mAh g-1 with an excellent high-rate cycling stability of 91.6% retention after 100 cycles, correspondingly the pristine shows 61.4 mAh g-1 and 73.1% retention.  These excellent electrochem. performances are ascribed to better structural stability, and lower charge transfer resistance and higher Na+ diffusion coeff. after Nb5+ doping.  Therefore, the Nb5+-doped P2-type cathode materials can be deemed as a beneficial improvement for researches on sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1149/1945-7111/acd43e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Koenig, G.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Revealing high Na-content P2-type layered oxides as advanced sodium-ion cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Chenglong; Yao, Zhenpeng; Wang, Qidi; Li, Haifeng; Wang, Jianlin; Liu, Ming; Ganapathy, Swapna; Lu, Yaxiang; Cabana, Jordi; Li, Baohua; Bai, Xuedong; Aspuru-Guzik, Alan; Wagemaker, Marnix; Chen, Liquan; Hu, Yong-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">142</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5742-5750</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered Na-based oxides with the general compn. of NaxTMO2 (TM: transition metal) have attracted significant attention for their high compositional diversity that provides tunable electrochem. performance for electrodes in sodium-ion batteries.  The various compns. bring forward complex structural chem. that is decisive for the layered stacking structure, Na-ion cond., and the redox activity, potentially promising new avenues in functional material properties.  In this work, we have explored the max. Na content in P2-type layered oxides and discovered that the high-content Na in the host enhances the structural stability; moreover, it promotes the oxidn. of low-valent cations to their high oxidn. states (in this case Ni2+).  This can be rationalized by the increased hybridization of the O(2p)-TM(3d-eg*) states, affecting both the local TM environment as well as the interactions between the NaO2 and TMO2 layers.  These properties are highly beneficial for the Na storage capabilities as required for cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  It leads to excellent Na-ion mobility, a large storage capacity (&gt;100 mAh g-1 between 2.0-4.0 V), yet preventing the detrimental sliding of the TMO2 layers (P2-O2 structural transition), as reflected by the ultralong cycle life (3000 (dis)charge cycles demonstrated).  These findings expand the horizons of high Na-content P2-type materials, providing new insights of the electronic and structural chem. for advanced cathode materials.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1088/2752-5724/ac8ab9"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">P2-type layered high-entropy oxides as sodium-ion cathode materials</span>. <i>Materials Futures</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>1</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">035104</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of cobalt-doped sodium lithium manganese oxide with superior rate capability and excellent cycling performance for sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thi Thu Hoa, Nguyen; Van Ky, Nguyen; Trung Son, Luong; Tien Dung, Dinh; Van Nguyen, To; Dinh Lam, Vu; Van Nghia, Nguyen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, cobalt-doped sodium lithium manganese oxide (NLMC) was synthesized by a solid-state reaction method. The NLMC material was delivers a specific capacity of 112 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.1C; up to higher c.d. of 1C, it has retained a specific capacity of 63 mAh/g.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Niobium-doped layered cathode material for high-power and low-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi Qinhao; Feng Xiaochen; Li Yong; Wang Xuan; Li Qianqian; Zhang Jiujun; Zhao Yufeng; Qi Ruijuan; Wang Jing; Yao Zhenpeng; Lu Xionggang; Zhang Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3205</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of sodium-based batteries in grid-scale energy storage requires electrode materials that facilitate fast and stable charge storage at various temperatures.  However, this goal is not entirely achievable in the case of P2-type layered transition-metal oxides because of the sluggish kinetics and unfavorable electrode electrolyte interphase formation.  To circumvent these issues, we propose a P2-type Na0.78Ni0.31Mn0.67Nb0.02O2 (P2-NaMNNb) cathode active material where the niobium doping enables reduction in the electronic band gap and ionic diffusion energy barrier while favoring the Na-ion mobility.  Via physicochemical characterizations and theoretical calculations, we demonstrate that the niobium induces atomic scale surface reorganization, hindering metal dissolution from the cathode into the electrolyte.  We also report the testing of the cathode material in coin cell configuration using Na metal or hard carbon as anode active materials and ether-based electrolyte solutions.  Interestingly, the Na  P2-NaMNNb cell can be cycled up to 9.2 A g(-1) (50 C), showing a discharge capacity of approximately 65 mAh g(-1) at 25 °C.  Furthermore, the Na  P2-NaMNNb cell can also be charged/discharged for 1800 cycles at 368 mA g(-1) and -40 °C, demonstrating a capacity retention of approximately 76% and a final discharge capacity of approximately 70 mAh g(-1).</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201411788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Layered P2- and O3-Type Composite as a High-Energy Cathode for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structure, Electrochemical, and Transport Properties of Li- and F-Modified P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 Cathode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Xinglong; Guo, Wenyue; Li, Rui; Du, Peng; Zhan, Xiaowen; Gao, Shan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Coatings</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">626</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">MDPI AG</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The development of cobalt-free P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathodes is hampered by poor electrochem. performance, resulting from structural instability during high-voltage cycling.  Herein, Li+ and F- ions are introduced simultaneously via a simple sol-gel method.  The F not only enters the lattice but forms chem. stable NaF on the surface.  The modified electrode delivered significantly better electrochem. performance than the pristine one, including much-enhanced capacity retention (64% vs. 36%, 100 cycles) at 0.5 C and a four-time higher capacity output at 10 C.  The ex situ XRD and in situ Raman anal. revealed cyclability enhancement mechanisms in terms of inhibiting the P2-O2 phase transition and Na+/vacancy ordering.  The cond. measurements (based on AC impedance and DC polarization) and GITT anal. proved, on both bulk material and electrode levels, that Na+ conduction and, thus, rate performance is notably promoted by doping.  The individual contribution of Li and F to the overall performance improvement was also discussed.  Furthermore, a solid-state sodium-metal battery was successfully demonstrated with the modified cathode.  The above results verify that Li+/F- incorporation can enable enhancements in both cyclability and rate capability of the P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 cathodes and are expected to provide a new perspective for the rational design of high-performance layered oxide cathode materials for progressive sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref58" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1002/cey2.518"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Marlton, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The effect of salt anion in ether-based electrolyte for electrochemical performance of sodium-ion batteries: A case study of hard carbon</span>. <i>Carbon Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2024</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e518</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1021/acsomega.8b01407"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Piriya, V. S. A.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Synergistic Role of Electrolyte and Binder for Enhanced Electrochemical Storage for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Omega</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>3</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">9945</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9955</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsomega.8b01407</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D9945-9955%26journal%3DACS%2BOmega%26issue%3D8%26author%3DV.%2BS.%2BA.%2BPiriya%26title%3DSynergistic%2BRole%2Bof%2BElectrolyte%2Band%2BBinder%2Bfor%2BEnhanced%2BElectrochemical%2BStorage%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsomega.8b01407&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.4c06248&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsomega.8b01407&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synergistic Role of Electrolyte and Binder for Enhanced Electrochemical Storage for Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Piriya, V. S. Ajay; Shende, Rashmi Chandrabhan; Seshadhri, G. Meenakshi; Ravindar, Dharavath; Biswas, Sanjay; Loganathan, Sadhasivam; Balasubramanian, T. S.; Rambabu, K.; Kamaraj, M.; Ramaprabhu, Sundara</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9945-9955</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACSODF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2470-1343</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium ion batteries are promising futuristic large-scale energy storage devices because of the abundant resources and low cost of sodium.  However, the development and commercialization of the sodium ion battery solely depends on the use of high capacity electrode materials.  Among the various metal oxides, SnO2 has high theor. specific capacity for sodium ion battery.  However, the enormous vol. expansion and low elec. cond. of SnO2 hinders its capability to reach the predicted theor. value.  Though different nanostructured designs of electrode materials like SnO2 nanocomposites have been studied, the effect of other cell components like electrolyte and binder to the specific capacity and cyclic stability are yet to be understood.  In the present study, we have investigated the synergistic effect of electrolyte and binder on the performance enhancement of SnO2 supported on an intertwined network structure of a reduced graphene oxide-partially open multiwalled carbon nanotube hybrid (rGPNT) as an anode in a sodium ion battery.  Our result shows that sodium carboxyl Me cellulose and ethylene carbonate: di-Et carbonate as the electrolyte solvent offers a high specific capacity of 688 mAh g-1 and a satisfactory cyclic stability for 500 cycles.  This is about 56% enhancement in specific capacity when compared to the use of polyvinylidene fluoride binder and propylene carbonate as the electrolyte solvent.  The present study provides a better understanding of synergistic role of electrolyte and binder for the development of metal oxides-based electrode materials for the advancement of the commercialization of sodium ion battery.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref60" class="refNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit60" data-doi="10.1149/1945-7111/ac5c41"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, J.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Effect of Electrolytes on the Cathode-Electrolyte Interfacial Stability of Fe-Based Layered Cathodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Electrochem. Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>169</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">3</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">030536</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/1945-7111/ac5c41</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D169%26publication_year%3D2022%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectrochem.%2BSoc.%26issue%3D3%26author%3DJ.%2BPark%26title%3DEffect%2Bof%2BElectrolytes%2Bon%2Bthe%2BCathode-Electrolyte%2BInterfacial%2BStability%2Bof%2BFe-Based%2BLayered%2BCathodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1149%252F1945-7111%252Fac5c41&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.4c06248&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F1945-7111%2Fac5c41&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of electrolytes on the cathode-electrolyte interfacial stability of Fe-based layered cathodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Jehee; Ku, Kyojin; Son, Seoung-Bum; Gim, Jihyeon; Kim, Youngsik; Lee, Eungje; Johnson, Christopher</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">169</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">030536</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JESOAN</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1945-7111</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">IOP Publishing Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Iron (Fe)-based layered oxide cathodes that employ Fe3+/Fe4+ redox reaction present a family of attractive cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries as iron is abundant, low-cost, and environmentally benign.  However, their electrochem. performance is not yet satisfactory and requires further improvement.  In this study, we investigate the effect of electrolytes on the electrochem. performance of α-NaFeO2, a prototypical model of Fe-based layered cathodes.  First, we established the crit. impact of the poor cathode-electrolyte interfacial stability on cell performances.  Systematic electrochem. tests and material characterizations further revealed the degrdn. mechanism in which the highly reactive Fe4+ state in the charged Na1-xFeO2 electrodes promotes severe electrolyte decompn. and subsequent growth of a thick interface layer that leads to impedance rise and performance degrdn.  In addn., the superior performance of NaPF6 over NaClO4 and the beneficial effect of the FEC additive are reported.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref61" class="refNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit61" data-doi="10.1016/j.ijhydene.2015.12.090"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vignarooban, K.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Current trends and future challenges of electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Int. J. Hydrogen Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>41</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">2829</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2846</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.ijhydene.2015.12.090</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D41%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D2829-2846%26journal%3DInt.%2BJ.%2BHydrogen%2BEnergy%26issue%3D4%26author%3DK.%2BVignarooban%26title%3DCurrent%2Btrends%2Band%2Bfuture%2Bchallenges%2Bof%2Belectrolytes%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.ijhydene.2015.12.090&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsomega.4c06248&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.ijhydene.2015.12.090&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Current trends and future challenges of electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Vignarooban, K.; Kushagra, R.; Elango, A.; Badami, P.; Mellander, B.-E.; Xu, X.; Tucker, T. G.; Nam, C.; Kannan, A. M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">International Journal of Hydrogen Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">41</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2829-2846</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">IJHEDX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0360-3199</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Research and development efforts on sodium-ion batteries are gaining momentum due to their potential to accommodate high energy d. coupled with relatively lower cost in comparison with lithium-ion batteries.  In order for the sodium-ion batteries to be com. viable, high performance electrolytes with acceptable ambient temp. ionic cond. and wider electrochem. stability windows are being developed.  A bibliometric anal. of the publications on various types of Na+ ion conducting electrolytes since 1990 shows a total of 200 + publications and reveals an exponential growth in the last few years, due to reasons that the sodium-ion systems promise great potential as the future large scale power sources for variety of applications.  This review consolidates the status of liq. (non-aq., aq. and ionic), polymer gel and solid (ceramics, glasses, and solid polymers) electrolytes and discusses their ionic cond., thermal characteristics, electrochem. stability and viscosity towards applications in sodium-ion batteries.  Among various types available, the non-aq. solvent based electrolyte is the most promising one in terms of ionic cond. even though it is flammable.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref62" class="refNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit62" data-doi="10.1002/cssc.202102522"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Z.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Optimizing the Electrolyte Systems for Na3(VO1-PO4)2F1 + 2 (0 ≤ <i>x</i> ≤ 1) Cathode and Understanding their Interfacial Chemistries Towards High-Rate Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ChemSusChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">8</span>), <span class="NLM_elocation-id">e202102522</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>46</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">12</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">3529</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3614</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6CS00776G</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2022.03.039"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Understanding rechargeable magnesium ion batteries via first-principles computations: A comprehensive review</span>. <i>Energy Storage Materials</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>48</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">344</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">355</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered transition metal compds. have attracted much attention due to their high theor. capacity and energy d. for sodium ion batteries. Here, using synchrotron-based operando transmission X-ray microscopy and high-energy X-ray diffraction combined with electrochem. measurements, the visualization of the dissym. phase transformation and structure evolution mechanism of layered NaNiO2 material during initial charge and discharge cycles are clarified.  Phase transformation and deformation of NaNiO2 during the voltage range of below 3.0 V and over 4.0 V are responsible for the irreversible capacity loss during the first cycling, which is also confirmed by the evolution of reaction kinetics behavior obtained by the galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A layered sodium manganese oxide, Na0.6MnO2, stable at temps. &gt;800°, was synthesized by using a sol-gel method that employs Mn(acac)3 (ac = acetylacetonate), Na2CO3, and propionic acid to form the resin framework.  This layered bronze possesses a hexagonal, P2-type structure, in which the distortion assocd. with Mn3+ is hardly noticeable.  It reacts slowly, though reversibly, with atm. moisture, which causes the interlayer spacing in the structure to increase by ∼2.5 Å, by intercalation of water mols. into the interlayer gap occupied by Na+ ions.  The anhyd. material was tested as a cathode in sodium cells.  Although the electrochem. intercalation of Na+ occurs in two steps, the host retains its main structural features, with a slight tendency in the interlayer spacing to contract as the sodium content increases.  The similarity between the discharge and charge profiles of the first cycles reveals a quasi-reversible nature of the intercalation process and that the cell can deliver a const. sp. capacity of ∼140 A-h/kg at 0.1 mA/cm2 when cycled in a voltage region of 3.8-2.0 V.  However, the continuous strains and distortions resulting from the insertion and extn. of Na+ ions cause the host structure to gradually collapse and yield an amorphous material after the first eight cycles.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a more sustainable alternative to the existing lithium-ion technol. and could alleviate some of the stress on the global lithium market as a result of the growing elec. car and portable electronics industries.  Fundamental research focused on understanding the structural and electronic processes occurring on electrochem. cycling is key to devising rechargeable batteries with improved performance.  We present an in-depth investigation of the effect of Mg doping on the electrochem. performance and structural stability of Na2/3MnO2 with a P2 layer stacking by comparing three compns.: Na2/3Mn1-yMgyO2 (y = 0.0, 0.05, 0.1).  We show that Mg substitution leads to smoother electrochem., with fewer distinct electrochem. processes, improved rate performance and better capacity retention.  These observations are attributed to the more gradual structural changes upon charge and discharge, as obsd. with synchrotron, powder X-ray, and neutron diffraction.  Mg doping reduces the no. of Mn3+ Jahn-Teller centers and delays the high voltage phase transition occurring in P2-Na2/3MnO2.  The local structure is investigated using 23Na solid-state NMR (ssNMR) spectroscopy.  The ssNMR data provide direct evidence for fewer oxygen layer shearing events, leading to a stabilized P2 phase, and an enhanced Na-ion mobility up to 3.8 V vs.  Na+/Na upon Mg doping.  The 5% Mg-doped phase exhibits one of the best rate performances reported to date for sodium-ion cathodes with a P2 structure, with a reversible capacity of 106 mA h g-1 at the very high discharge rate of 5000 mA g-1.  In addn., its structure is highly reversible and stable cycling is obtained between 1.5 and 4.0 V vs.  Na+/Na, with a capacity of approx. 140 mA h g-1 retained after 50 cycles at a rate of 1000 mA g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1007/s10008-023-05706-4"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Zinc doped P2-type layered cathode for high-voltage and long-life sodium ion batteries: impacts of calcination temperature and cooling methods</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Though P2-type Na-Mn-Ni-O cathodes with low cost and environmental benign were extensively studied, it is still challenging to fulfill practical application with limited cycle stability and low operating potential.  However, the research of the reactive Ni2+/Ni3+ redox pair that enable both high working potential and high reversible capacity was almost ignored.  And traditional cationic doping mainly focuses on crystal modulation and structure stabilization.  An anion doping strategy (F-doping) was carried out to further boost the activity of Ni2+.  The multi-function including structural parameter modulation and robust Ni-F bond significantly promote the activation of Ni2+/Ni3+ and advance the resp. working potential.  Related reaction kinetics and structural evolution were also studied to elucidate the F-doping mechanism.  The Na0.6Mn0.95Ni0.05O1.95F0.05 with appropriate F content could deliver a high capacity of 80.76 mA h g-1 at 2C with 75.0% retained after 960 cycles.  The excellent rate capability and full cell performance also demonstrate the high potential.  This study may provide a new sight for the development of P2-type layered Na-Mn-Ni-O cathode, which could be extended to other oxides cathode.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1016/j.jssc.2021.122440"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">First-principles investigation on the crystal, electronic structures and diffusion barriers of F-doped NaMO2 (M = V, Cr, Co and Ni) for rechargeable Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>J.     </div><div class="casAbstract">A structural refinement method for neutron diffraction is presented which makes direct use of the profile intensities obtained from the powder diagram.  It is applicable to nuclear structures and to magnetic structures which can be described on the nuclear unit cell or a multiple thereof.  Equations for the measured profiles to be used in the least sqs. treatment are cor. for asymmetry and preferred orientation; the angular dependence of the half widths of the peaks is given by the formula of Caglioti, et al. (1958).  The magnetic contribution to the profile equation is expressed by calcg. only one av. cross section for each set of equiv. reflections.  It is possible to introduce constraint functions, linear or quadratic, between parameters used in the least sqs. treatment.  Results of the use of this method are given for a series of compds.  In all instances it has proved superior to any other method involving integrated neutron powder intensities, single or overlapping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/0001-6160(53)90006-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Williamson, G.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Methods of analysis previously used in the interpretation of line broadening are discussed and are shown to be inadequate; more reliable methods being outlined.  An analysis of published results by one of these methods suggests that the observed effects can be attributed to simultaneous small particle size and strain broadening.  Measurements of the changes in intensity distribution have been made, with a Geiger counter spectrometer, in the spectra of cold-worked Al and W.  The line breadths may be attributed to simultaneous small particle size and strain broadening, the latter predominating, particularly at the higher Bragg angles, and it is shown that the observed effects are produced by dislocations or some similar structural fault.  The observed rise in the breadths of the high angle lines from annealed materials suggests that some dislocations remain after annealing.         </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type layered oxides based on the elements Fe and Mn have attracted great interest as sodium ion battery (SIB) cathode materials owing to their inexpensive metal constituents and high specific capacity.  However, they suffer from rapid capacity fading and complicated phase transformations.  Here, we modulate the crystal structure and optimize the electrochem. performances of Na0.67Mn0.5Fe0.5O2 by Al doping for Mn or Fe, resp., and the roles of Al in the enhancement of the rate capability and cycling performance are unraveled.  The substitution of Al for Mn or Fe decreases the lattice parameters a and c but enlarges d spacing and lengthens Na-O bonds, which enhances Na+ diffusion and rate capability esp. for Na0.67Mn0.5Fe0.47Al0.03O2.  Al doping reduces the thickness of TMO2 and strengthens TM-O/O-O bonding.  This enhances the layered structure stability and the capacity retention.  Al doping mitigates Mn3+ and Jahn-Teller distortion, mitigating the irreversible phase transition.  Al doping also alleviates the lattice vol. variation and the structure strain.  This further improves the stability of the layered structure and the cycling performances particularly in the case of Al doping for Fe.  The in-depth insights into the roles of Al substitution might be also useful for designing high-performance cathode materials for SIBs through appropriate lattice doping.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref45"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref45" class="rightTabRefNumLink">45</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit45" data-doi="10.1039/D1TA05137G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Soares, C.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na2.4Al0.4Mn2.6O7 anionic redox cathode material for sodium-ion batteries – a combined experimental and theoretical approach to elucidate its charge storage mechanism</span>. <i>Journal of Materials Chemistry A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">13</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">7341</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7356</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">142</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered Na-based oxides with the general compn. of NaxTMO2 (TM: transition metal) have attracted significant attention for their high compositional diversity that provides tunable electrochem. performance for electrodes in sodium-ion batteries.  The various compns. bring forward complex structural chem. that is decisive for the layered stacking structure, Na-ion cond., and the redox activity, potentially promising new avenues in functional material properties.  In this work, we have explored the max. Na content in P2-type layered oxides and discovered that the high-content Na in the host enhances the structural stability; moreover, it promotes the oxidn. of low-valent cations to their high oxidn. states (in this case Ni2+).  This can be rationalized by the increased hybridization of the O(2p)-TM(3d-eg*) states, affecting both the local TM environment as well as the interactions between the NaO2 and TMO2 layers.  These properties are highly beneficial for the Na storage capabilities as required for cathode materials in sodium-ion batteries.  It leads to excellent Na-ion mobility, a large storage capacity (&gt;100 mAh g-1 between 2.0-4.0 V), yet preventing the detrimental sliding of the TMO2 layers (P2-O2 structural transition), as reflected by the ultralong cycle life (3000 (dis)charge cycles demonstrated).         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, cobalt-doped sodium lithium manganese oxide (NLMC) was synthesized by a solid-state reaction method.  Crystal structure and morphol. of the NLMC material were examd. using X-ray diffraction, selected area electron diffraction, scanning eletron microscopy, transmission electron microscopy, energy dispersive spectroscopy, and inductively coupled plasma - optical emission spectrometry anal.  The NLMC material was utilized to fabricate CR2032-type coin cells, and later evaluated for its electrochem. characteristics.  The partial substitution of manganese ions in the structure by cobalt and lithium ions is the main reason for the outstanding electrochem. properties.  The NLMC material was delivers a specific capacity of 112 mAh/g at a c.d. of 0.1C; up to higher c.d. of 1C, it has retained a specific capacity of 63 mAh/g. The presented results provide new pathway of obtaining high electrochem. performance of the sodium manganese-based materials by employing other transitional elements to partially substitute manganese in the crystal structure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-022-30942-z"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Niobium-doped layered cathode material for high-power and low-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Nat.
